deposedKey states.DeposedKey) error {\n528: \tchanges := ctx.Changes()\n529: \n530: \tif change == nil {\n531: \t\t// Caller sets nil to indicate that we need to remove a change from\n532: \t\t// the a refresh for a resource\n580: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) refresh(ctx EvalContext, deposedKey states.DeposedKey, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject) (*states.ResourceInstanceObject, ret, diags\n723: }\n724: \n725: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n726: \tctx EvalContext,\n727: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n728: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n729: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n730: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n731: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n732: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n733: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n734: \n735: \tresource := n.Addr.Resource.Resource\n736: \t// If we plan to write or delete sensitive paths from state,\n1200: \t// this is an Update action.\n1201: \t//\n1202: \t// We need to filter out any marks which may not apply to the new planned\n1203: \t// value before comparison. The one case where a provider is allowed to\n1204: \t// return a different value from the configuration is when a config change\n1205: \t// is not functionally significant and the prior state can be returned. If a\n1206: \t// new mark was also discarded from that config change, it needs to be\n1207: \t// ignored here to prevent an errant update action.\n1208: \tif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n1209: \t\taction = plans.Update\n1210: \t}\n1211: \n1212: \t// As a special case, if we have a previous diff (presumably from the plan\n1213: \t// phases, whereas we're now in the apply phase) and it was for a replace,\n1214: \t// we've already deleted the original object from state by the time we\n1215: \t// get here and so we would've ended up with a _create_ action this time,\n1216: \t// which we now need to paper over to get a result consistent with what\n1217: \t// we originally intended.\n1218: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n1219: \t\tprevChange := *plannedChange\n1220: \t\tif prevChange.Action.IsReplace() && action == plans.Create {\n1221: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] plan: %s treating Create change as %s change to match with earlier plan\", n.Addr, prevChange.Action)\n1222: \t\t\taction = prevChange.Action\n1223: \t\t\tpriorVal = prevChange.Before\n1224: \t\t}\n1225: \t}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n1228: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n1229: \t\treturn h.PostDiff(n.Addr, addrs.NotDeposed, action, priorVal, plannedNewVal)\n1230: \t}))\n1231: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1232: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1233: \t}\n1234: \n1235: \t// Update our return plan\n1236: \tplan := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1237: \t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1238: \t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1239: \t\tPrivate:      plannedPrivate,\n1240: \t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1241: \t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1242: \t\t\tAction: action,\n1243: \t\t\tBefore: priorVal,\n1244: \t\t\t// Pass the marked planned value through in our change\n1245: \t\t\t// to propogate through evaluation.\n1246: \t\t\t// Marks will be removed when encoding.\n1247: \t\t\tAfter:           plannedNewVal,\n1248: \t\t\tGeneratedConfig: n.generatedConfigHCL,\n1249: \t\t},\n1250: \t\tActionReason:    actionReason,\n1251: \t\tRequiredReplace: reqRep,\n1252: \t}\n1253: \n1254: \t// Update our return state\n1255: \tstate := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1256: \t\t// We use the special \"planned\" status here to note that this\n1257: \t\t// object's value is not yet complete. Objects with this status\n1258: \t\t// cannot be used during expression evaluation, so the caller\n1259: \t\t// must _also_ record the returned change in the active plan,\n1260: \t\t// which the expression evaluator will use in preference to this\n1261: \t\t// incomplete value recorded in the state.\n1262: \t\tStatus:  states.ObjectPlanned,\n1263: \t\tValue:   plannedNewVal,\n1264: \t\tPrivate: plannedPrivate,\n1265: \t}\n1266: \n1267: \treturn plan, state, keyData, diags\n1268: }\n1269: \n1270: func (n *NodeAbstractResource) processIgnoreChanges(prior, config cty.Value, schema *configschema.Block) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1271: \t// ignore_changes only applies when an object already exists, since we\n1272: \t// can't ignore changes to a thing we've not created yet.\n1273: \tif prior.IsNull() {\n1274: \t\treturn config, nil\n1275: \t}\n1276: \n1277: \tignoreChanges := traversalsToPaths(n.Config.Managed.IgnoreChanges)\n1278: \tignoreAll := n.Config.Managed.IgnoreAllChanges\n1279: \n1280: \tif len(ignoreChanges) == 0 && !ignoreAll {\n1281: \t\treturn config, nil\n1282: \t}\n1283: \n1284: \tif ignoreAll {\n1285: \t\t// Legacy providers need up to clean up their invalid plans and ensure\n1286: \t\t// no changes are passed though, but that also means making an invalid\n1287: \t\t// config with computed values. In that case we just don't supply a\n1288: \t\t// schema and return the prior val directly.\n1289: \t\tif schema == nil {\n1290: \t\t\treturn prior, nil\n1291: \t\t}\n1292: \n1293: \t\t// If we are trying to ignore all attribute changes, we must filter\n1294: \t\t// computed attributes out from the prior state to avoid sending them\n1295: \t\t// to the provider as if they were included in the configuration.\n1296: \t\tret, _ := cty.Transform(prior, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1297: \t\t\tattr := schema.AttributeByPath(path)\n1298: \t\t\tif attr != nil && attr.Computed && !attr.Optional {\n1299: \t\t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n1300: \t\t\t}\n1301: \n1302: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1303: \t\t})\n1304: \n1305: \t\treturn ret, nil\n1306: \t}\n1307: \n1308: \tif prior.IsNull() || config.IsNull() {\n1309: \t\t// Ignore changes doesn't apply when we're creating for the first time.\n1310: \t\t// Proposed should never be null here, but if it is then we'll just let it be.\n1311: \t\treturn config, nil\n1312: \t}\n1313: \n1314: \tret, diags := processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config, ignoreChanges)\n1315: \n1316: \treturn ret, diags\n1317: }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = path\n1326: \t}\n1327: \treturn paths\n1328: }\n1329: \n1330: func traversalToPath(traversal hcl.Traversal) cty.Path {\n1331: \tpath := make(cty.Path, len(traversal))\n1332: \tfor si, step := range traversal {\n1333: \t\tswitch ts := step.(type) {\n1334: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseRoot:\n1335: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1336: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1337: \t\t\t}\n1338: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseAttr:\n1339: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1340: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1341: \t\t\t}\n1342: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseIndex:\n1343: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.IndexStep{\n1344: \t\t\t\tKey: ts.Key,\n1345: \t\t\t}\n1346: \t\tdefault:\n1347: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unsupported traversal step %#v\", step))\n1348: \t\t}\n1349: \t}\n1350: \treturn path\n1351: }\n1352: \n1353: func processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1354: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1355: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1356: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1357: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1358: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1359: \t\t// key index.\n1360: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1361: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1362: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1363: \t}\n1364: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1365: \n1366: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1367: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1368: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1369: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1370: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1371: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1372: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1373: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1374: \t\tif ok {\n1375: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1376: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1377: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1378: \t\t\t}\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \n1381: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1382: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. Any other intermediate index error\n1383: \t\t// means we wouldn't be able to apply the value below, so no need to\n1384: \t\t// record this.\n1385: \t\tp, err := icPath.Apply(prior)\n1386: \t\tif err != nil {\n1387: \t\t\tcontinue\n1388: \t\t}\n1389: \t\tc, err := icPath.Apply(config)\n1390: \t\tif err != nil {\n1391: \t\t\tcontinue\n1392: \t\t}\n1393: \n1394: \t\t// If this is a map, it is checking the entire map value for equality\n1395: \t\t// rather than the individual key. This means that the change is stored\n1396: \t\t// here even if our ignored key doesn't change. That is OK since it\n1397: \t\t// won't cause any changes in the transformation, but allows us to skip\n1398: \t\t// breaking up the maps and checking for key existence here too.\n1399: \t\tif !p.RawEquals(c) {\n1400: \t\t\t// there a change to ignore at this path, store the prior value\n1401: \t\t\tignoredValues = append(ignoredValues, ignoreChange{icPath, p, key})\n1402: \t\t}\n1403: \t}\n1404: \n1405: \tif len(ignoredValues) == 0 {\n1406: \t\treturn config, nil\n1407: \t}\n1408: \n1409: \tret, _ := cty.Transform(config, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1410: \t\t// Easy path for when we are only matching the entire value. The only\n1411: \t\t// values we break up for inspection are maps.\n1412: \t\tif !v.Type().IsMapType() {\n1413: \t\t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1414: \t\t\t\tif path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1415: \t\t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1416: \t\t\t\t}\n1417: \t\t\t}\n1418: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1419: \t\t}\n1420: \t\t// We now know this must be a map, so we need to accumulate the values\n1421: \t\t// key-by-key.\n1422: \n1423: \t\tif !v.IsNull() && !v.IsKnown() {\n1424: \t\t\t// since v is not known, we cannot ignore individual keys\n1425: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1426: \t\t}\n1427: \n1428: \t\t// The map values will remain as cty values, so we only need to store\n1429: \t\t// the marks from the outer map itself\n1430: \t\tv, vMarks := v.Unmark()\n1431: \n1432: \t\t// The configMap is the current configuration value, which we will\n1433: \t\t// mutate based on the ignored paths and the prior map value.\n1434: \t\tvar configMap map[string]cty.Value\n1435: \t\tswitch {\n1436: \t\tcase v.IsNull() || v.LengthInt() == 0:\n1437: \t\t\tconfigMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1438: \t\tdefault:\n1439: \t\t\tconfigMap = v.AsValueMap()\n1440: \t\t}\n1441: \n1442: \t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1443: \t\t\tif !path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1444: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1445: \t\t\t}\n1446: \n1447: \t\t\tif ignored.key.IsNull() {\n1448: \t\t\t\t// The map address is confirmed to match at this point,\n1449: \t\t\t\t// so if there is no key, we want the entire map and can\n1450: \t\t\t\t// stop accumulating values.\n1451: \t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1452: \t\t\t}\n1453: \t\t\t// Now we know we are ignoring a specific index of this map, so get\n1454: \t\t\t// the config map and modify, add, or remove the desired key.\n1455: \n1456: \t\t\t// We also need to create a prior map, so we can check for\n1457: \t\t\t// existence while getting the value, because Value.Index will\n1458: \t\t\t// return null for a key with a null value and for a non-existent\n1459: \t\t\t// key.\n1460: \t\t\tvar priorMap map[string]cty.Value\n1461: \n1462: \t\t\t// We need to drop the marks from the ignored map for handling. We\n1463: \t\t\t// don't need to store these, as we now know the ignored value is\n1464: \t\t\t// only within the map, not the map itself.\n1465: \t\t\tignoredVal, _ := ignored.value.Unmark()\n1466: \n1467: \t\t\tswitch {\n1468: \t\t\tcase ignored.value.IsNull() || ignoredVal.LengthInt() == 0:\n1469: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1470: \t\t\tdefault:\n1471: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = ignoredVal.AsValueMap()\n1472: \t\t\t}\n1473: \n1474: \t\t\tkey := ignored.key.AsString()\n1475: \t\t\tpriorElem, keep := priorMap[key]\n1476: \n1477: \t\t\tswitch {\n1478: \t\t\tcase !keep:\n1479: \t\t\t\t// this didn't exist in the old map value, so we're keeping the\n1480: \t\t\t\t// \"absence\" of the key by removing it from the config\n1481: \t\t\t\tdelete(configMap, key)\n1482: \t\t\tdefault:\n1483: \t\t\t\tconfigMap[key] = priorElem\n1484: \t\t\t}\n1485: \t\t}\n1486: \n1487: \t\tvar newVal cty.Value\n1488: \t\tswitch {\n1489: \t\tcase len(configMap) > 0:\n1490: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapVal(configMap)\n1491: \t\tcase v.IsNull():\n1492: \t\t\t// if the config value was null, and no values remain in the map,\n1493: \t\t\t// reset the value to null.\n1494: \t\t\tnewVal = v\n1495: \t\tdefault:\n1496: \t\t\tnewVal = cty.MapValEmpty(v.Type().ElementType())\n1497: \t\t}\n1498: \n1499: \t\tif len(vMarks) > 0 {\n1500: \t\t\tnewVal = newVal.WithMarks(vMarks)\n1501: \t\t}\n1502: \n1503: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1504: \t})\n1505: \treturn ret, nil\n1506: }\n1507: \n1508: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1509: // A previously evaluated configVal can be passed in, or a new one is generated\n1510: // from the resource configuration.\n1511: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) readDataSource(ctx EvalContext, configVal cty.Value) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1512: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1513: \tvar newVal cty.Value\n1514: \n1515: \tconfig := *n.Config\n1516: \n1517: \tprovider, resource lifecycle:\n1674: // either actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1675: //\n1676: // currentState is the current state for the data source, and the new state is\n1677: // returned. While data sources are read-only, we need to start with the prior\n1678: // state to determine if we have a change or not.  If we needed to read a new\n1679: // value, but it still matches the previous state, then we can record a NoNop\n1680: // change. If the states don't match then we record a Read change so that the\n1681: // new value is applied to the state.\n1682: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) planDataSource(ctx EvalContext, checkRuleSeverity tfdiags.Severity, skipPlanChanges bool) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, instances.RepetitionData, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1683: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n1684: \tvar keyData instances.RepetitionData\n1685: \tvar configVal cty.Value\n1686: \n1687: \t_, providerSchema, err := getProvider(ctx, n.ResolvedProvider)\n1688: \tif err != providerSchema.SchemaForResourceAddr(n.Addr.ContainingResource().Resource)\n1694: \tif schema == nil {\n1695: \t\t// Should be caught during validation, so we don't bother with a pretty error here\n1696: \t\tdiags = diags.Append(fmt.Errorf(\"provider %q does not support data source %q\", n.ResolvedProvider, n.Addr.ContainingResource().Resource.Type))\n1697: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1698: \t}\n1699: \n1700: \tobjTy := schema.ImpliedType()\n1701: \tpriorVal := cty.NullVal(objTy)\n1702: \n1703: \tforEach, _ := evaluateForEachExpression(config.ForEach, ctx)\n1704: \tkeyData = EvalDataForInstanceKey(n.ResourceInstanceAddr().Resource.Key, forEach)\n1705: \n1706: \tcheckDiags := evalCheckRules(\n1707: \t\taddrs.ResourcePrecondition,\n1708: \t\tn.Config.Preconditions,\n1709: \t\tctx, n.Addr, keyData,\n1710: \t\tcheckRuleSeverity,\n1711: \t)\n1712: \tdiags = diags.Append(checkDiags)\n1713: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1714: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags // failed n.nestedInCheckBlock()\n1725: \tif nested {\n1726: \t\t// Going forward from this point, the only reason we will fail is\n1727: \t\t// that the data source fails to load its data. Normally, this would\n1728: \t\t// cancel the entire plan and this error message would bubble its way\n1729: \t\t// back up to the user.\n1730: \t\t//\n1731: \t\t// But, if we are in a check block then we don't want this data block to\n1732: \t\t// cause the plan to fail. We also need to report a status on the data\n1733: \t\t// block so the check processing later on knows whether to attempt to\n1734: \t\t// process the checks. Either we'll report the data block as failed\n1735: \t\t// if/when we load the data block later, or we want to report it as a\n1736: \t\t// success overall.\n1737: \t\t//\n1738: \t\t// Therefore, we create a deferred function here that will check if the\n1739: \t\t// status for the check has been updated yet, and if not we will set it\n1740: \t\t// to be StatusPass. The rest of this function will only update the\n1741: \t\t// status if it should be StatusFail.\n1742: \t\tdefer func() {\n1743: \t\t\tstatus := ctx.Checks().ObjectCheckStatus(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module))\n1744: \t\t\tif status == checks.StatusUnknown {\n1745: \t\t\t\tctx.Checks().ReportCheckResult(check.Addr().Absolute(n.Addr.Module), addrs.CheckDataResource, 0, checks.StatusPass)\n1746: \t\t\t}\n1747: \t\t}()\n1748: \t}\n1749: \n1750: \tconfigKnown := planDataSource: %s configuration not fully known yet, so deferring to apply phase\", n.Addr)\n1772: \t\t\treason = plans.ResourceInstanceReadBecauseConfigUnknown\n1773: \t\tcase depsPending:\n1774: main part of the data resource lifecycle: either\n1956: // actually reading from the data source or generating a plan to do so.\n1957: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyDataSource(ctx (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) evalApplyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, createNew bool, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2059: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2060: \n2061: \tif state == nil {\n2062: \t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] evalApplyProvisioners: %s has no state, so skipping provisioners\", n.Addr)\n2063: \t\treturn nil\n2064: []*configs.Provisioner {\n2108: \t// Fast path the zero case\n2109: \tif config == nil || config.Managed == nil {\n2110: \t\treturn nil\n2111: \t}\n2112: \n2113: \tif len(config.Managed.Provisioners) \t\tif p.When == when {\n2120: \t\t\tresult = append(result, p)\n2121: \t\t}\n2122: \t}\n2123: \n2124: \treturn result\n2125: }\n2126: \n2127: // applyProvisioners executes the provisioners for a resource.\n2128: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, when configs.ProvisionerWhen, provs []*configs.Provisioner) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2129: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2130: \n2131: \t// this self is only used for destroy provisioner evaluation, and must\n2132: \t// refer to the last known value of the // object associated with a resource instance. In practice not all remote\n17: // objects are actually remote in the sense of being accessed over the network,\n18: // but this is the most common case.\n19: //\n20: // It is not valid to mutate a ResourceInstanceObject once it has been created.\n21: // Instead, create a new object and replace the existing one.\n22: type ResourceInstanceObject struct {\n23: \t// Value is the object-typed value representing the remote object within\n24: \t// Terraform.\n25: \tValue cty.Value\n26: \n27: \t// Private is an opaque value set by the provider when this object was\n28: \t// last created or updated. Since it cannot be moved into the\\n64: \\t// ObjectRead state, a tainted object must be replaced.\\n65: \\tObjectTainted ObjectStatus = 'T'\\n66: \\n67: \\t// ObjectPlanned is a special object status used only for the transient\\n68: \\t// placeholder objects we place into state during the refresh and plan\\n69: \\t// walks to stand in for objects that will be created during apply.\\n70: \\t//\\n71: \\t// Any object of this status must have a corresponding change recorded\\n72: \\t// in the current plan, whose value must then be used in preference to\\n73: \\t// the value stored in state when evaluating expressions. When a resource is refreshed (line 620-626 of node_resource_abstract_instance.go):\n   - The prior value is unmarked and marks are extracted as `priorPaths`\n   - Provider returns unmarked response\n   - Then at line 718-720, the marks are reapplied\n\n2. But the marks only include marks from SENSITIVE VARIABLES (var.db_password is marked sensitive), not from the SCHEMA (provider schema says password field is always sensitive)\n\n3. When encoding to state (instance_object.go line 98), only the marks present in the value are saved to `AttrSensitivePaths`\n\n4. When decoding from state (instance_object_src.go line 89-90), the saved marks are reapplied\n\n5. When evaluating expressions (evaluate.go line 714-723), the code applies schema marks if the schema contains sensitive attributes, combining them with marks from state\n\nThis creates an asymmetry:\n- State has marks from sensitive variables only\n- When read via GetResource during planning, schema marks are added (lines 714-723)\n- But the plan doesn't go through GetResource for the current state\n- The plan path uses the prior value directly without schema marks\n- So the planned value has schema marks applied (when reading from plan), but the prior value doesn't\n- This causes a difference in marks that looks like a change\n\nLet me verify this by looking at how the plan compares values. The issue is that priorVal in the plan method (line 869) is unmarked and doesn't get schema marks applied, while plannedNewVal gets schema marks applied if the config had sensitive variable references.\n\nActually, looking more closely at line 995-1000, the marks reapplied are just from the config (unmarkedPaths from line 868), not from the schema. But then when this change is written to state via writeChange (line 564), it goes through change.Encode which only saves marks that are actually in the value.\n\n\nThe core issue is that during refresh, only variable-based marks persist to state, while schema-based marks get added dynamically during evaluation. Line 446-449: For the \"after\" value, it does the same thing\n\nThe problem is that `rc.BeforeValMarks` and `rc.AfterValMarks` come from the change that was encoded. The change was created in node_resource_abstract_instance.go plan() method:\n\n- `Before` = `priorVal` (with marks from priorPaths - which are from the state, which only has variable marks)\n- `After` = `plannedNewVal` (with marks from unmarkedPaths - which are from the config)\n\nWhen the change is encoded, those marks are extracted and saved as BeforeValMarks and AfterValMarks. Then when they're decoded, those same marks are reapplied.\n\nBUT, the issue is that at lines 418 and 447, the code adds schema marks when generating JSON output. This happens for BOTH before and after values.\n\nSo if priorVal didn't have schema marks (because they weren't stored in state), but the schema says those attributes are sensitive, then:\n- The JSON output will show schema marks for the Before value\n- This makes it look like the Before and After are different in terms of sensitivity\n- Even if the underlying values are identical\n\nThe root cause is that when state is stored after a refresh (in the refresh() method at line 719), the marks reapplied are only from `priorPaths`, which don't include schema-defined sensitive marks. But when JSON output is generated, schema marks are added on-the-fly. This creates a mismatch between what's stored in the plan and what's displayed in JSON output.\n\n\nThe solution would involve ensuring schema marks are persisted to the state during encoding, rather than being applied only during JSON generation. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01LbGGmDLVMETi4MMbXrPVeU","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"tool_use","id":"toolu_012mn9ScYdgpRSbe1xkkHDDR","name":"Write","input":{"file_path":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place update diffs for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because of an asymmetry in how sensitivity marks flow through the system. The issue stems from **incomplete sensitivity mark persistence in state**: when resource values are refreshed and stored, only marks from sensitive variable references are saved, not marks from the provider schema itself. During plan generation, schema marks are applied dynamically to the JSON output for display purposes, creating an apparent difference in sensitivity between before and after values even though the underlying attribute values are identical.\n\n---\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Incomplete sensitivity mark storage at state serialization boundary.**\n\nThe root cause is located in the **state refresh-to-storage pipeline**, specifically:\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, `refresh()` method (lines 620-722)**: When a resource is refreshed from the provider, marks extracted before sending to the provider (`priorPaths` at line 625) only contain marks from sensitive variables (e.g., `var.db_password` marked as sensitive). These are **not** the provider schema's declared sensitive attributes.\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`, `Encode()` method (line 98)**: When encoding the refreshed value for storage, `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` extracts **only the marks currently on the value**. Since schema-defined sensitive marks were never added to the refreshed value (the provider returns unmarked values and only variable marks are reapplied), the schema marks are **not** present in the encoded state.\n\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`, `Decode()` method (lines 89-90)**: When decoding from state, only the marks that were stored (`AttrSensitivePaths`) are reapplied. These lack schema-defined marks.\n\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`, `GetResource()` method (lines 714-723)**: This is the **compensating workaround** that masks the underlying issue. When reading resource values for expression evaluation during planning, the code explicitly applies schema marks if the schema contains sensitive attributes. This creates the asymmetry: values read **via GetResource** have schema marks added, but values read **directly from state** in the plan path do not.\n\n5. **`internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`, `MarshalResourceChange()` method (lines 417-420, 446-449)**: When generating JSON output for display, schema marks are applied on-the-fly to both before and after values. This compounds the issue: the before value appears to have sensitivity marks that were never stored in the plan itself.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**1. Refresh Path – Incomplete Mark Extraction (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:620-722)**\n\n```go\n// Line 623-626: Extract marks BEFORE sending to provider\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n// priorPaths only contains marks from sensitive variables, NOT schema\n\n// Line 717-720: Reapply marks AFTER provider returns\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n// Schema marks are NOT reapplied here\n```\n\n**Issue**: `priorPaths` only has marks from sensitive variable references. Provider schema declares sensitive attributes are never added at this point.\n\n---\n\n**2. State Encoding – Missing Schema Marks (instance_object.go:94-137)**\n\n```go\nfunc (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    // Line 98: Extract existing marks\n    val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n    // ... process value ...\n\n    // Line 131: Save only the marks that are on the value\n    AttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,  // Missing schema marks!\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: Only marks present in the value are persisted. Schema-defined sensitive marks are never in the value because the refresh path never adds them.\n\n---\n\n**3. State Decoding – Restore Incomplete Marks (instance_object_src.go:77-104)**\n\n```go\nfunc (os *ResourceInstanceObjectSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceObject, error) {\n    val, err := ctyjson.Unmarshal(os.AttrsJSON, ty)\n    if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n        val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)  // Only has variable marks\n    }\n    return &ResourceInstanceObject{Value: val, ...}, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: Reapplies only the incomplete marks that were stored.\n\n---\n\n**4. Evaluator Compensation – Schema Marks Applied at Expression Evaluation Time (evaluate.go:714-723)**\n\n```go\n// When reading from state for planned resources (lines 714-723)\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)  // ADD schema marks here\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\ninstances[key] = val\n```\n\n**Issue**: This is a compensating mechanism that adds schema marks during **evaluation** (when reading from state for expression purposes), but these marks are **not** part of the planned change or state storage. This is the ONLY place schema marks are applied in the normal flow.\n\n---\n\n**5. JSON Output Generation – Dynamic Schema Mark Addition (jsonplan/plan.go:417-420, 446-449)**\n\n```go\n// For Before value (line 417-425):\nmarks := rc.BeforeValMarks  // Only has variable marks from the plan\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.Before, nil)...)  // Add schema marks here\n}\nbs := jsonstate.SensitiveAsBool(changeV.Before.MarkWithPaths(marks))\nbeforeSensitive, err := ctyjson.Marshal(bs, bs.Type())\n\n// For After value (line 446-449):\nmarks := rc.AfterValMarks  // Only has variable marks from the plan\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.After, nil)...)  // Add schema marks here\n}\nas := jsonstate.SensitiveAsBool(changeV.After.MarkWithPaths(marks))\nafterSensitive, err := ctyjson.Marshal(as, as.Type())\n```\n\n**Issue**: Schema marks are applied at JSON output time, making the before value appear to have sensitivity information that was never persisted in the plan. The difference in before vs. after sensitivity (in marks only, not in values) appears as a change to the user.\n\n---\n\n**6. Plan Phase – Incomplete Mark Comparison (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208-1210)**\n\n```go\n// Check if marks differ even though values are equal\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: This compares `unmarkedPaths` (marks from config) against `priorPaths` (marks from state, missing schema marks). Neither has schema marks, so for schema-sensitive attributes with no variable marks, they appear equal when they shouldn't.\n\n---\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** – Refresh path, plan path:\n   - `refresh()` method: Extracts and reapplies incomplete marks\n   - `plan()` method: Uses incomplete marks for comparison\n   - Does not apply schema marks to prior values\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** – State serialization:\n   - `Encode()` method: Serializes incomplete marks to state file\n\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** – State deserialization:\n   - `Decode()` method: Restores incomplete marks from state\n\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** – Expression evaluation:\n   - `GetResource()` method: Applies schema marks when reading state for evaluation (compensating mechanism)\n\n5. **`internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`** – JSON plan output:\n   - `MarshalResourceChange()` method: Dynamically applies schema marks at output time\n\n6. **`internal/terraform/marks.go`** – Utility functions:\n   - `marksEqual()`: Used for comparing incomplete mark sets\n   - `filterMarks()`: Filters inapplicable marks\n\n---\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n```\n1. User sees \"will be updated in-place\" for resource with sensitive schema attributes\n   ↓\n3. terraform show -json shows different sensitive_values in before vs. after\n   ↓\n4. Root cause: Sensitivity metadata differs between before and after in JSON output\n   ↓\n5. Before sensitivity: Includes schema marks (added at JSON output time)\n   After sensitivity: Includes schema marks (added at JSON output time)\n   Both appear different because schema marks were never in the planned change\n   ↓\n6. Why schema marks are missing from planned change:\n   a) Refresh returns unmarked value from provider\n   b) Only variable-reference marks are reapplied (line 719)\n   c) State is encoded with incomplete marks (line 98)\n   d) Plan reads state with incomplete marks (lines 89-90)\n   e) Plan's BeforeValMarks only have variable marks, not schema marks\n   ↓\n7. Why GetResource compensates:\n   - GetResource explicitly applies schema marks when reading from state (line 714-723)\n   - This is ONLY mechanism adding schema marks in normal flow\n   - But these marks are NOT captured in the plan itself\n   ↓\n8. Why phantom diff appears:\n   - JSON output generation applies schema marks on-the-fly (lines 418-420, 446-449)\n   - Before value: Has dynamically-applied schema marks\n   - After value: Has dynamically-applied schema marks\n   - But from different sources (refreshed state vs. provider response)\n   - Even though underlying values are identical, mark structure differs\n   ↓\n9. Why it only affects schema-sensitive attributes:\n   - Variable marks are preserved in state\n   - Schema marks are NOT preserved in state\n   - So only schema-sensitive attributes (without variable marks) lack marks in state\n   ↓\n10. ROOT CAUSE: Asymmetry in mark persistence\n    - Sensitive variables: Marks persisted in state ✓\n    - Schema sensitive attributes: Marks NOT persisted in state ✗\n    - Compensating layer (GetResource) masks issue during evaluation\n    - JSON generation exposes issue by dynamically adding missing marks\n```\n\n---\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe fix requires **ensuring schema-defined sensitive marks are persisted in state**, not applied only during evaluation or output generation.\n\n**Two approaches:**\n\n**Option A (Preferred): Apply schema marks at state encoding time**\n- Modify `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`'s `refresh()` method to apply schema marks before encoding\n- At line 717-720, after reapplying variable marks, also apply schema marks\n- This ensures state encodes complete sensitivity information\n- State decoding will then have complete marks\n- Eliminates need for compensating layer in evaluate.go\n- Eliminates dynamic mark application in JSON output\n\n**Option B: Capture schema marks in plan**\n- Modify `plan()` method to explicitly apply schema marks to `priorVal`\n- Encode schema marks into `BeforeValMarks` when creating the change\n- This ensures the planned change has complete mark information\n- Still requires changes to how marks are compared and stored\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. **Enable trace logging** in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`:\n   - Log `priorPaths` extracted at line 625\n   - Log marks on value after reapplying at line 719\n   - Compare against schema.ValueMarks() to see what's missing\n\n2. **Inspect state file** after refresh:\n   ```bash\n   terraform state show -json <resource> | jq '.current_state_object.sensitive_attributes'\n   ```\n   - Will only show paths for variable-marked attributes\n   - Should include schema-marked paths\n\n3. **Compare plan marks**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform show -json <plan-file> | jq '.resource_changes[].change | {before_sensitive, after_sensitive}'\n   ```\n   - Before will have no schema marks (from state)\n   - After will have schema marks (from evaluate.go)\n   - Difference indicates the phantom update\n\n4. **Test with schema-sensitive only** vs. **variable-sensitive only** attributes:\n   - Schema-sensitive-only: Phantom diff appears\n   - Variable-sensitive-only: No phantom diff (marks persisted)\n\n---\n\n## Additional Context\n\n### Why GetResource Compensates\n\nThe `GetResource()` method in `evaluate.go` (lines 714-723) is a **defensive compensating layer**. It ensures that when Terraform evaluates expressions that reference resource values from state, those values have schema-defined sensitivity marks applied. This prevents sensitive attributes from being accidentally logged or displayed during evaluation.\n\nHowever, **this compensation only applies to expression evaluation**, not to:\n- Plan change storage (`BeforeValMarks`, `AfterValMarks`)\n- State storage (`AttrSensitivePaths`)\n- Plan file output\n\n### Why JSON Output Exposes the Issue\n\nThe `jsonplan/plan.go` code (lines 418-420, 446-449) applies schema marks **at output time** because:\n1. It reads `BeforeValMarks` and `AfterValMarks` from the change, which have incomplete marks\n2. It detects the incompleteness via `schema.ContainsSensitive()`\n3. It dynamically adds missing schema marks for display purposes\n\nThis is a **second compensating layer** that only helps with JSON output, not with the core issue of incomplete mark persistence.\n\n### Historical Context\n\nThis design pattern suggests that at some point, the `GetResource()` compensation was sufficient. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_012mn9ScYdgpRSbe1xkkHDDR","type":"tool_result","content":"File created successfully at: /logs/agent/investigation.md"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ddd6e96d-7473-4de5-8b6d-ac0c2680b650","uuid":"9187842e-7c02-45b3-9eb0-04cc6dbaa889","tool_use_result":{"type":"create","filePath":"/logs/agent/investigation.md","content":"# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place update diffs for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because of an asymmetry in how sensitivity marks flow through the system. The issue stems from **incomplete sensitivity mark persistence in state**: when resource values are refreshed and stored, only marks from sensitive variable references are saved, not marks from the provider schema itself. During plan generation, schema marks are applied dynamically to the JSON output for display purposes, creating an apparent difference in sensitivity between before and after values even though the underlying attribute values are identical.\n\n---\n\n## Root Cause\n\n**Incomplete sensitivity mark storage at state serialization boundary.**\n\nThe root cause is located in the **state refresh-to-storage pipeline**, specifically:\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, `refresh()` method (lines 620-722)**: When a resource is refreshed from the provider, marks extracted before sending to the provider (`priorPaths` at line 625) only contain marks from sensitive variables (e.g., `var.db_password` marked as sensitive). These are **not** the provider schema's declared sensitive attributes.\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`, `Encode()` method (line 98)**: When encoding the refreshed value for storage, `UnmarkDeepWithPaths()` extracts **only the marks currently on the value**. Since schema-defined sensitive marks were never added to the refreshed value (the provider returns unmarked values and only variable marks are reapplied), the schema marks are **not** present in the encoded state.\n\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`, `Decode()` method (lines 89-90)**: When decoding from state, only the marks that were stored (`AttrSensitivePaths`) are reapplied. These lack schema-defined marks.\n\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`, `GetResource()` method (lines 714-723)**: This is the **compensating workaround** that masks the underlying issue. When reading resource values for expression evaluation during planning, the code explicitly applies schema marks if the schema contains sensitive attributes. This creates the asymmetry: values read **via GetResource** have schema marks added, but values read **directly from state** in the plan path do not.\n\n5. **`internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`, `MarshalResourceChange()` method (lines 417-420, 446-449)**: When generating JSON output for display, schema marks are applied on-the-fly to both before and after values. This compounds the issue: the before value appears to have sensitivity marks that were never stored in the plan itself.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### Code References\n\n**1. Refresh Path – Incomplete Mark Extraction (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:620-722)**\n\n```go\n// Line 623-626: Extract marks BEFORE sending to provider\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n// priorPaths only contains marks from sensitive variables, NOT schema\n\n// Line 717-720: Reapply marks AFTER provider returns\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n// Schema marks are NOT reapplied here\n```\n\n**Issue**: `priorPaths` only has marks from sensitive variable references. Provider schema declares sensitive attributes are never added at this point.\n\n---\n\n**2. State Encoding – Missing Schema Marks (instance_object.go:94-137)**\n\n```go\nfunc (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    // Line 98: Extract existing marks\n    val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n    // ... process value ...\n\n    // Line 131: Save only the marks that are on the value\n    AttrSensitivePaths:  pvm,  // Missing schema marks!\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: Only marks present in the value are persisted. Schema-defined sensitive marks are never in the value because the refresh path never adds them.\n\n---\n\n**3. State Decoding – Restore Incomplete Marks (instance_object_src.go:77-104)**\n\n```go\nfunc (os *ResourceInstanceObjectSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceObject, error) {\n    val, err := ctyjson.Unmarshal(os.AttrsJSON, ty)\n    if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n        val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)  // Only has variable marks\n    }\n    return &ResourceInstanceObject{Value: val, ...}, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: Reapplies only the incomplete marks that were stored.\n\n---\n\n**4. Evaluator Compensation – Schema Marks Applied at Expression Evaluation Time (evaluate.go:714-723)**\n\n```go\n// When reading from state for planned resources (lines 714-723)\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)  // ADD schema marks here\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\ninstances[key] = val\n```\n\n**Issue**: This is a compensating mechanism that adds schema marks during **evaluation** (when reading from state for expression purposes), but these marks are **not** part of the planned change or state storage. This is the ONLY place schema marks are applied in the normal flow.\n\n---\n\n**5. JSON Output Generation – Dynamic Schema Mark Addition (jsonplan/plan.go:417-420, 446-449)**\n\n```go\n// For Before value (line 417-425):\nmarks := rc.BeforeValMarks  // Only has variable marks from the plan\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.Before, nil)...)  // Add schema marks here\n}\nbs := jsonstate.SensitiveAsBool(changeV.Before.MarkWithPaths(marks))\nbeforeSensitive, err := ctyjson.Marshal(bs, bs.Type())\n\n// For After value (line 446-449):\nmarks := rc.AfterValMarks  // Only has variable marks from the plan\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(changeV.After, nil)...)  // Add schema marks here\n}\nas := jsonstate.SensitiveAsBool(changeV.After.MarkWithPaths(marks))\nafterSensitive, err := ctyjson.Marshal(as, as.Type())\n```\n\n**Issue**: Schema marks are applied at JSON output time, making the before value appear to have sensitivity information that was never persisted in the plan. The difference in before vs. after sensitivity (in marks only, not in values) appears as a change to the user.\n\n---\n\n**6. Plan Phase – Incomplete Mark Comparison (node_resource_abstract_instance.go:1208-1210)**\n\n```go\n// Check if marks differ even though values are equal\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Issue**: This compares `unmarkedPaths` (marks from config) against `priorPaths` (marks from state, missing schema marks). Neither has schema marks, so for schema-sensitive attributes with no variable marks, they appear equal when they shouldn't.\n\n---\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** – Refresh path, plan path:\n   - `refresh()` method: Extracts and reapplies incomplete marks\n   - `plan()` method: Uses incomplete marks for comparison\n   - Does not apply schema marks to prior values\n\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** – State serialization:\n   - `Encode()` method: Serializes incomplete marks to state file\n\n3. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** – State deserialization:\n   - `Decode()` method: Restores incomplete marks from state\n\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** – Expression evaluation:\n   - `GetResource()` method: Applies schema marks when reading state for evaluation (compensating mechanism)\n\n5. **`internal/command/jsonplan/plan.go`** – JSON plan output:\n   - `MarshalResourceChange()` method: Dynamically applies schema marks at output time\n\n6. **`internal/terraform/marks.go`** – Utility functions:\n   - `marksEqual()`: Used for comparing incomplete mark sets\n   - `filterMarks()`: Filters inapplicable marks\n\n---\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n```\n1. SYMPTOM: terraform plan shows phantom in-place update even with no config changes\n   ↓\n2. User sees \"will be updated in-place\" for resource with sensitive schema attributes\n   ↓\n3. terraform show -json shows different sensitive_values in before vs. after\n   ↓\n4. Root cause: Sensitivity metadata differs between before and after in JSON output\n   ↓\n5. Before sensitivity: Includes schema marks (added at JSON output time)\n   After sensitivity: Includes schema marks (added at JSON output time)\n   Both appear different because schema marks were never in the planned change\n   ↓\n6. Why schema marks are missing from planned change:\n   a) Refresh returns unmarked value from provider\n   b) Only variable-reference marks are reapplied (line 719)\n   c) State is encoded with incomplete marks (line 98)\n   d) Plan reads state with incomplete marks (lines 89-90)\n   e) Plan's BeforeValMarks only have variable marks, not schema marks\n   ↓\n7. Why GetResource compensates:\n   - GetResource explicitly applies schema marks when reading from state (line 714-723)\n   - This is ONLY mechanism adding schema marks in normal flow\n   - But these marks are NOT captured in the plan itself\n   ↓\n8. Why phantom diff appears:\n   - JSON output generation applies schema marks on-the-fly (lines 418-420, 446-449)\n   - Before value: Has dynamically-applied schema marks\n   - After value: Has dynamically-applied schema marks\n   - But from different sources (refreshed state vs. provider response)\n   - Even though underlying values are identical, mark structure differs\n   ↓\n9. Why it only affects schema-sensitive attributes:\n   - Variable marks are preserved in state\n   - Schema marks are NOT preserved in state\n   - So only schema-sensitive attributes (without variable marks) lack marks in state\n   ↓\n10. ROOT CAUSE: Asymmetry in mark persistence\n    - Sensitive variables: Marks persisted in state ✓\n    - Schema sensitive attributes: Marks NOT persisted in state ✗\n    - Compensating layer (GetResource) masks issue during evaluation\n    - JSON generation exposes issue by dynamically adding missing marks\n```\n\n---\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe fix requires **ensuring schema-defined sensitive marks are persisted in state**, not applied only during evaluation or output generation.\n\n**Two approaches:**\n\n**Option A (Preferred): Apply schema marks at state encoding time**\n- Modify `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`'s `refresh()` method to apply schema marks before encoding\n- At line 717-720, after reapplying variable marks, also apply schema marks\n- This ensures state encodes complete sensitivity information\n- State decoding will then have complete marks\n- Eliminates need for compensating layer in evaluate.go\n- Eliminates dynamic mark application in JSON output\n\n**Option B: Capture schema marks in plan**\n- Modify `plan()` method to explicitly apply schema marks to `priorVal`\n- Encode schema marks into `BeforeValMarks` when creating the change\n- This ensures the planned change has complete mark information\n- Still requires changes to how marks are compared and stored\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. **Enable trace logging** in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`:\n   - Log `priorPaths` extracted at line 625\n   - Log marks on value after reapplying at line 719\n   - Compare against schema.ValueMarks() to see what's missing\n\n2. **Inspect state file** after refresh:\n   ```bash\n   terraform state show -json <resource> | jq '.current_state_object.sensitive_attributes'\n   ```\n   - Will only show paths for variable-marked attributes\n   - Should include schema-marked paths\n\n3. **Compare plan marks**:\n   ```bash\n   terraform show -json <plan-file> | jq '.resource_changes[].change | {before_sensitive, after_sensitive}'\n   ```\n   - Before will have no schema marks (from state)\n   - After will have schema marks (from evaluate.go)\n   - Difference indicates the phantom update\n\n4. **Test with schema-sensitive only** vs. **variable-sensitive only** attributes:\n   - Schema-sensitive-only: Phantom diff appears\n   - Variable-sensitive-only: No phantom diff (marks persisted)\n\n---\n\n## Additional Context\n\n### Why GetResource Compensates\n\nThe `GetResource()` method in `evaluate.go` (lines 714-723) is a **defensive compensating layer**. It ensures that when Terraform evaluates expressions that reference resource values from state, those values have schema-defined sensitivity marks applied. This prevents sensitive attributes from being accidentally logged or displayed during evaluation.\n\nHowever, **this compensation only applies to expression evaluation**, not to:\n- Plan change storage (`BeforeValMarks`, `AfterValMarks`)\n- State storage (`AttrSensitivePaths`)\n- Plan file output\n\n### Why JSON Output Exposes the Issue\n\nThe `jsonplan/plan.go` code (lines 418-420, 446-449) applies schema marks **at output time** because:\n1. It reads `BeforeValMarks` and `AfterValMarks` from the change, which have incomplete marks\n2. It detects the incompleteness via `schema.ContainsSensitive()`\n3. It dynamically adds missing schema marks for display purposes\n\nThis is a **second compensating layer** that only helps with JSON output, not with the core issue of incomplete mark persistence.\n\n### Historical Context\n\nThis design pattern suggests that at some point, the `GetResource()` compensation was sufficient.
